<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>

<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>

<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>

<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>
<s> viii to the daisy to the same flower and the green linnet' all composed at town end orchard where the bird was often seen as here described <\s>
<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>

<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>

<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>

<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>

<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>

<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>

<s> to the small celandine <\s>

<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>

<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>

<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>

<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> xxvii in dora's field 1833 rydal mount <\s>
<s> this nest was built as described in a tree that grows near the pool in dora's field next the rydal mount garden <\s>
<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>
<s> viii to the daisy to the same flower and the green linnet' all composed at town end orchard where the bird was often seen as here described <\s>
<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>
<s> what adds much to the interest that attends it is its habit of shutting itself up and opening out according to the degree of light and temperature of the air <\s>
<s> in pencil on opposite page has not chaucer noticed it note common pilewort <\s>
<s> the story of this poem is from the german of frederica brun <\s>

<s> xxii written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>

<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>

<s> to the small celandine <\s>

<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>

<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>

<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>
<s> viii to the daisy to the same flower and the green linnet' all composed at town end orchard where the bird was often seen as here described <\s>
<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>
<s> what adds much to the interest that attends it is its habit of shutting itself up and opening out according to the degree of light and temperature of the air <\s>
<s> in pencil on opposite page has not chaucer noticed it note common pilewort <\s>
<s> the story of this poem is from the german of frederica brun <\s>
<s> the redbreast chasing the butterfly <\s>
<s> xv observed as described in the then beautiful orchard at town end <\s>
<s> song for the spinning wheel <\s>
<s> the belief on which this is founded i have often heard expressed by an old neighbour of grasmere <\s>
<s> hint from the mountains <\s>
<s> xvii bunches of fern may often be seen wheeling about in the wind as here described <\s>
<s> the particular bunch that suggested these verses was noticed in the pass of dunmail raise <\s>
<s> the verses were composed in 1817 but the application is for all times and places <\s>

<s> this parrot belonged to mrs <\s>
<s> luff while living at fox ghyll <\s>
<s> the wren was one that haunted for many years the summer house between the two terraces at rydal mount <\s>

<s> xxii written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>

<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>

<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>
<s> viii to the daisy to the same flower and the green linnet' all composed at town end orchard where the bird was often seen as here described <\s>
<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>
<s> what adds much to the interest that attends it is its habit of shutting itself up and opening out according to the degree of light and temperature of the air <\s>

<s> xxii written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>

<s> to the small celandine <\s>

<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>

<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>

<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>
<s> viii to the daisy to the same flower and the green linnet' all composed at town end orchard where the bird was often seen as here described <\s>
<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>

<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>

<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>

<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>

<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> this nest was built as described in a tree that grows near the pool in dora's field next the rydal mount garden <\s>
<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>

<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>

<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>

<s> to the small celandine <\s>

<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>

<s> xxvii in dora's field 1833 rydal mount <\s>
<s> this nest was built as described in a tree that grows near the pool in dora's field next the rydal mount garden <\s>
<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>
<s> viii to the daisy to the same flower and the green linnet' all composed at town end orchard where the bird was often seen as here described <\s>
<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>
<s> what adds much to the interest that attends it is its habit of shutting itself up and opening out according to the degree of light and temperature of the air <\s>

<s> xxii written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>
<s> in pencil on opposite page dora 117 <\s>
<s> xxvii in dora's field 1833 rydal mount <\s>
<s> this nest was built as described in a tree that grows near the pool in dora's field next the rydal mount garden <\s>
<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> broom grows under it and in many places on the side of the precipice <\s>
<s> vi written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>
<s> to the same flower <\s>
<s> viii to the daisy to the same flower and the green linnet' all composed at town end orchard where the bird was often seen as here described <\s>
<s> to the small celandine <\s>
<s> it is remarkable that this flower coming out so early in the spring as it does and so bright and beautiful and in such profusion should not have been noticed earlier in english verse <\s>
<s> what adds much to the interest that attends it is its habit of shutting itself up and opening out according to the degree of light and temperature of the air <\s>

<s> xxii written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>
<s> in pencil on opposite page dora 117 <\s>
<s> xxvii in dora's field 1833 rydal mount <\s>
<s> this nest was built as described in a tree that grows near the pool in dora's field next the rydal mount garden <\s>
<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> vii this poem and two others to the same flower were written in the year 1802 which is mentioned because in some of the ideas though not in the manner in which those ideas are connected and likewise even in some of the expressions there is a resemblance to passages in a poem lately published of mr <\s>
<s> james montgomery's entitled a field flower <\s>
<s> this being said mr <\s>
<s> montgomery will not think any apology due to him but i cannot however help addressing him in the words of the father of english poets though it happe me to rehersin that ye han in your freshe songes saied forberith me and beth not ill apaied sith that ye se i doe it in the honour of love and eke in service of the flour <\s>
<s> note see in chaucer and the older poets the honours formerly paid to this flower <\s>

<s> to the small celandine <\s>

<s> xxii written in germany 1799 <\s>
<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>
<s> in pencil on opposite page dora 117 <\s>
<s> xxvii in dora's field 1833 rydal mount <\s>
<s> this nest was built as described in a tree that grows near the pool in dora's field next the rydal mount garden <\s>
<s> xxviii it has been said that the english though their country has produced so many great poets is now the most unpoetical nation in europe <\s>
<s> it is probably true for they have more temptation to become so than any other european people <\s>
<s> the rotha mentioned in the poem is the river which flowing through the lakes of grasmere and ryedale falls into wynandermere <\s>
<s> on helmcrag that impressive single mountain at the head of the vale of grasmere is a rock which from most points of view bears a striking resemblance to an old woman cowering <\s>
<s> close by this rock is one of those fissures or caverns which in the language of the country are called dungeons <\s>
<s> most of the mountains here mentioned immediately surround the vale of grasmere of the others some are at a considerable distance but they belong to the same cluster <\s>
<s> there is an eminence c iii 1800 <\s>
<s> it is not accurate that the eminence here alluded to could be seen from our orchard seat <\s>
<s> it arises above the road by the side of grasmere lake towards keswick and its name is stone arthur <\s>
<s> a narrow girdle of rough stones and crags iv point kash judgment last line <\s>
<s> the character of the eastern shore of grasmere lake is quite changed since these verses were written by the public road being carried along its side <\s>
<s> the friends spoken of were coleridge and my sister and the fact occurred strictly as recorded <\s>
<s> v two years before our marriage <\s>
<s> the pool alluded to is in rydal upper park <\s>
<s> when to the attractions c vi 1805 <\s>
<s> the grove still exists but the plantation has been walled in and is not so accessible as when my brother john wore the path in the manner here described <\s>
<s> the grove was a favourite haunt with us all while we lived at town end <\s>
<s> when we and others whom we love shall meet a second time in grasmere's happy vale last lines <\s>
<s> this wish was not granted the lamented person not long after perished by shipwreck in discharge of his duty as commander of the honourable east india company's vessel the earl of abergavenny <\s>

<s> it was entirely a fancy but intended as a prelude to a ballad poem never written <\s>
<s> song for the wandering jew <\s>
<s> xxiv suggested on the thames by the sight of one of those floating mills that used to be seen there <\s>
<s> this i noticed on the surrey side between somerset house and blackfriars bridge <\s>
<s> charles lamb was with me at the time and i thought it remarkable that i should have to point out to him an idolatrous londoner a sight so interesting as the happy group dancing on the platform <\s>
<s> mills of this kind used to he and perhaps still are not uncommon on the continent <\s>
<s> i noticed several upon the river saone in the year 1799 particularly near the town of chalons where my friend jones and i halted a day when we crossed france so far on foot <\s>
<s> there we embarked and floated down to lyons <\s>
<s> the pilgrim's dream or the star and the glowworm <\s>
<s> xxv i distinctly recollect the evening when these verses were suggested in 1818 <\s>
<s> it was on the road between rydal and grasmere where glow worms abound <\s>
<s> a star was shining above the ridge of loughrigg fell just opposite <\s>
<s> i remember a blockhead of a critic in some review or other crying out against this piece <\s>
<s> what so monstrous said he as to make a star talk to a glowworm <\s>
<s> poor fellow we know well from this sage observation what the primrose on the river's brim was to him <\s>
<s> further in writing to coleridge he says i parted from m on monday afternoon about six o'clock a little on this side rushyford <\s>
<s> soon after i missed my road in the midst of the storm .... <\s>
<s> between the beginning of lord darlington's park at raby and two or three miles beyond staindrop i composed the poem on the opposite page the pilgrim's dream c <\s>
<s> i reached barnard castle about half past ten <\s>
<s> between eight and nine evening i reached eusemere <\s>
<s> the poet and the caged turtle dove <\s>
<s> xxvi rydal mount 1830 <\s>
<s> this dove was one of a pair that had been given to my daughter by our excellent friend miss jewsbury who went to india with her husband mr <\s>
<s> fletcher where she died of cholera <\s>
<s> the dove survived its mate many years and was killed to our great sorrow by a neighbour's cat that got in at the window and dragged it partly out of the cage <\s>
<s> these verses were composed extempore to the letter in the terrace summer house before spoken of <\s>
<s> it was the habit of the bird to begin cooing and murmuring whenever it heard me making my verses <\s>
